B007C4ZJ0S|4.0|With Cynthia Rothrock considered yesterday's news and the film world over-enamored with Milla Jovovich in her over-produced blockbusters, it really surprises me that a movie like \\"Haywire\\" could still be made under the Hollywood umbrella. Not only is an action movie starring a woman getting the big-name treatment, but it's an action movie starring a genuine fighter and not some stunt-doubled starlet. While most of the professional cage brawlers who've made it to the film world have had to slug it out in some remarkably bad low-budget fare (e.g. [[ASIN:B001RLW9Y6 Never Surrender]]), MMA heroine Gina Carano lucks out with a great director and a surprisingly good cast in a pretty satisfying CIA revenge flick that could easily become the foundation of a very promising career.<br /><br />The story: black ops operative Mallory Kane (Carano, who had a bit part in [[ASIN:B002FU8JTW Blood & Bone]]) embarks on an intercontinental mission to find out why she was betrayed by her allies...<br /><br />I can easily see why the general, non- action-oriented public might not like this movie. Director Steven Soderbergh is definitely one of contemporary Hollywood's best, and because this isn't [[ASIN:B000067IZ3 Traffic]], people who aren't in it for the punches and kicks might consider it a step down for him. Additionally, even I was surprised by this one's cast: I would have expected to find Channing Tatum ([[ASIN:B002E01LL6 Fighting]]), but Antonio Banderas ([[ASIN:0800130448 Desperado]]), Ewan McGregor ([[ASIN:B0057ZAA6W Trainspotting]]), and Michael friggin' Douglas ([[ASIN:B00003CXDB Wall Street]])? It's as though Steven Soderbergh called in some favors and bets he won... Truthfully, some of these big names aren't necessary to the film - Michael Douglas' role as a CIA director could've easily been played by someone else - so again, some viewers who will watch this film for name recognition are chancing disappointment when these big stars end up not doing too much. With that said, everybody generally does well and you have to hand it to star Gina Carano for making the most of her first major role: even when not kicking butt, her dramatic offering is more than acceptable.<br /><br />Of course, the main reason I saw the film was for the butt-kicking, and I'm pleased to say that I wasn't disappointed. Mixed martial arts movies contradict my belief that the best fight scenes are produced by low-budget fare where choreographical creativity can be embellished and not stifled by the whims of producers: while the majority of direct-to-video MMA movies have featured truly awful fight scenes, Hollywood seems to have a better bead on how to make the most of \\"realistic\\" fighting, and \\"Haywire\\" is a great example. Carano has six fights of varying lengths throughout the film, and to say that she uses them to redefine how powerful a woman can appear onscreen is an understatement. Even though I like only four of these brawls (which include a standup battle against Ewan McGregor of all people), they're good enough to make me reconsider the place of mixed martial arts in movies. The fights are, for the most part, well-shot and Carano displays the same sort of brutal efficiency as in her Strikeforce career, though she's not above the occasional flashy move like a rebounding roundhouse off the wall. When it comes to looking like she really means it but still being entertaining, Gina's got few equals.<br /><br />The production is strong, which should be a given in a Soderbergh movie. Some of the European scenes are shot on location, others are fudged, but it all looks authentic. The film doesn't try to do anything aesthetically new, but as far as I'm concerned, it doesn't need to: unless you're particularly needy of car chases and explosions, this movie delivers what an action picture should and does it with a complete lack of pretense. My only major qualm? - the ending comes from out of nowhere and bit too soon for my taste, but I can live with this. Definitelyworth a watch, and probably even a buy.worth a watch, and probably even a buy.

B005LAIH5O|3.0|It'd be difficult to approach Wrath of the Titans with a completely open mind. The film it follows, Clash of the Titans, was dull and almost single-handedly began the downfall of 3D in the US. Those low expectations though may actually be an advantage for Wrath. Though flawed it's an entertaining film with some spectacular special effects. Even more surprising - the 3D is worthwhile and enhances the experience.<br /><br />The story follows Perseus (Sam Worthington) who must travel into the underworld to rescue his father Zeus (Liam Neeson). Zeus' other son Ares (Edgar Ramirez) has turned on him and handed him over to Hades (Ralph Fiennes). The plan is to sap Zeus' powers and transfer them to the leader of the imprisoned Titans - Kronos - (father to Zeus, Hades, and Poseiden) who would then unleash hell on the world.<br /><br />Where the negativity towards Clash really makes an impact is in the early minutes of Wrath. There is no real emotional attachment to the characters - no real care for their fates or the conflicts that are at hand. I wasn't sure the film would be able to break out of that but it somehow did despite inherent confusion around their relationships and motivations without having Clash's plot fresh on the mind. It just took a little time for it to come together.<br /><br />Wrath of the Titans isn't going to win any awards for dialogue which is sketchy to say the least and almost laughable at times. In fact the movie tends to just move from one set piece to the next with the story taking a back seat. The action is what ties it all together and ultimately leads into a massive final battle. It was actually somewhat startling just was how brisk the pace was and how quickly events advanced - by the time that battle came around it didn't feel as though it was already time for the film to be concluded.<br /><br />That is a compliment as the first film was plodding and anything but an enjoyable experience. The effects in Wrath are extraordinary and the uniqueness of the various monsters, and the sheer size of Kronos, adds to the fun. While I rarely would recommend paying extra for 3D - and I still wouldn't necessarily with Wrath - there were some really cool moments that were taken advantage of with the technology and it added some valuable depth to scenes. All things being equal going with the 3D wouldn't be a bad decision here.<br /><br />Wrath of the Titans achieved something unanticipated - it entertained and even made the prospect of a third film in the series somewhat appealing. Expectations, albeit very low, were easily exceeded. There are better overall options in theaters right now (21 Jump Street, The Hunger Games) but for the crowd seeking action Wrath of the Titans is worth considering.eness of the various monsters, and the sheer size of Kronos, adds to the fun. 0393317552|4.0|Jared Diamond's 1998 Pulitzer Prize winning popular science book presents, in some circles, a controversial theme or even racist explanation for the differences in the development of societies over time. However, the author states early on \\"the modern world's inequalities: why did human development proceed at such different rates on different continents? Those disparate rates constitute history's broadest pattern and my books subject.\\" In addition, to counter the racist's question he states \\"History follows different courses for different people because of differences in environments, not because of biological difference\\"<br /><br />He proceeds in a well written logical progression to explain this thesis throughout the book starting with spread of humans around the world and the beginnings of civilization and the various rates at which they have developed. He proceeds to explain that there are four sets of factors which have caused the unequal speed and development of civilizations between the various continents. They are:<br /><br />1. Differences in the wild plants and animal species available for domestication.<br /><br />2. Factors affecting the rates of human diffusion and migration which differed greatly among continents.<br /><br />3. Diffusion between continents, which may also help build up and spread these domesticates and technology.<br /><br />4.  Continental differences in area or total population size which with a larger area or population gives that society more opportunity to develop.<br /><br />Which brings us to his main conclusion: \\"All human societies contain inventive people which speeds development. It's just that some environments provide more starting material and more favorable conditions for utilizing inventions, than do other environments.\\"<br /><br />You will not find footnotes in this book because it is popular science and not a scientific treatise. However, at the back of the book, you will find a well-organized Further Reading section if you want to dig into more detail of his presentation and concepts.<br /><br />Overall, the book presented well the themes, concepts and overall conclusions, which I had thought for years, to be the reasons for the differences in societies. Mr. Diamond just presented it in a better way !if you want to dig into more detail of his presentation and concepts.<br /><br />Overall, the book presented well the themes, concepts and overall conclusions, which I had thought for years, to be the reasons for the differences in societies. I am not a self-help junkie by any means, but I bought the book, let it sit and thought nothing more of it. As a realtor, times were tough in 2010. We were about dead broke, my income dropped over 75% in a year, and I saw no light at the end of the tunnel. We had been served with foreclosure papers, and I couldn't get a job to save my life, despite numerous attempts and interviews and an extensive background in the paralegal field. One day, I remembered I had this book. I was too depressed to even read it. A few more weeks went by and I kept thinking of it but something always stopped me from picking it up. Finally I did, and I read it in one sitting. I began by going to the website and printing off a Universal Bank blank check and filled in $100,000. Then I began practicing what I learned, and it wasn't easy to train my brain to quit with the negative and shift into what has become my daily internal chant, I have an abundance of money, health and happiness. The shift from \\"they won't buy a house\\" turned into \\"they will buy a house\\". Everytime I have quiet time, be it when I'm driving (I turn off the radio now) or home with no one around, I repeat that mantra over and over and I tell the \\"Universe\\" what I want. It may sound corny, but it WORKS. In 2011, our tax returned showed income of over $120,000 and for the first time ever, I made more than my husband. Then sales started to slow down again, funny how quickly we forget. I realized I had gotten away from practicing what I learned and began doing it again. The phone started ringing again, ideas came to me that I hadn't thought of before, and once again, sales were on the rise. So to you people on the fence, please don't listen to the people who are so quick to criticize; I am an average person with an average life and from the bottom of my heart, I truly believe the things I learned from this book saved us from foreclosure, allowedme to open a savings account and has been nothing short of a Godsend. It's not easy to train your mind to think differently and it's always a struggle, but with time, it does get easier. I think I get my best practice in the car when I'm alone. I've been asked by various realtor friends what I'm doing that caused my business to increase and I have to say I hesitate to tell them because I don't want them to think I\\"m loony, so when they say it's been a closely guarded secret for centuries, I believe it and I understand why. I don't think it's necessarily out of greed, I think it's because people are skeptical and quick to judge. But I felt compelled to share this because if just one person decides to try it and their life changes like mine did, then I have passed the secret on just like Rhonda did. She's not a manipulator, she knows what she's talking about. And give it time, it won't be instantaneous and you may not even realize it's all coming together until you sit back one day and think, wait a minute, things have gradually started to improve... could it be?? Yes, it is. Good luck to everyone and keep an open mind!

B004N7WJF0|4.0|Sometime during the 1990's, German heavy metal icons the Scorpions, seemed to have lost their enthusiasm for the genre.  Their album Face The Heat, released in 1993 was probably their last that was in the traditional heavy metal vein.  Subsequent albums [[ASIN:B000002JA5 Pure Instinct]] (1996) and [[ASIN:B00000J8NQ Eye II Eye]] (1999) reflected a change in style.  Although \\"You And I\\" from Pure Instinct is featured in the Acoustica performance, these albums have come to be largely ignored by the band.<br /><br />Still trying to find their way, in 2000 the band embarked on a project with the Berlin Philharmonic Orchestra, and conductor Christian Kolonovits, that eventually became [[ASIN:B0000584ZL The Scorpions - Moment of Glory (Live with the Berlin Philharmonic Orchestra)]] (2000), an event released on both CD and DVD.  Acoustica is a continuation of the band's excursion down an alternate musical path, as the Scorps are basically playing unplugged, taking part in a trend that had been quite popular during the 90's.  Christian Kolonovits again joins the band for this project, playing keyboards.  Other additional musicians include Johan Daansen on guitar, and Ariana Arcu on cello.<br /><br />Acoustica was recorded in Lisbon, Portugal, and features Rudolf Schenker and Matthias Jabs playing acoustic guitars.  Bass player Ralph Rieckermann, and drummer James Kottak, play their normal instruments.  While in an unusual situation, vocalist Klaus Meine is backed by three female singers.  The 21 song setlist includes classic Scorpions songs, cover tunes, and some brand new material.  The band put in a lot of effort into the performance, selecting the songs, writing new songs, developing the musical arrangements for acoustic instruments, and incorporating the other musicians into the project.<br /><br />In general, the results are very good, as the \\"unplugged\\" approach typically brings a fresh new appreciation for material normally featuring distorted electric guitars played at extreme volume.  The arrangement for \\"Catch Your Train\\" for example, gives the song a whole new vibe.  Almost everything sounds terrific, and the band is having a great time in a new musical arena.  Guitarists, Jabs and Schenker, probably have to make the biggest adjustment, and they handle the transition to acoustic quite smoothly.  Softer numbers like \\"Send Me An Angel\\", \\"Under the Same Sun\\", \\"You And I\\", and \\"Still Loving You\\", probably sound the closest to the studio versions, while \\"Holiday\\" is given a Latin feel.  Rockers like \\"Rhythm of Love\\", \\"The Zoo\\", \\"Loving You Sunday Morning\\", and a jazzy version of \\"Tease Me, Please Me\\", might sound the most interesting unplugged.  For \\"The Zoo\\" and \\"Tease Me, Please Me\\", a number of female dancers also join the proceedings.<br /><br />The new material generally works well in the acoustic format, and includes the songs \\"I Wanted To Cry\\", \\"Life Is Too Short\\", and \\"Back To You\\".  \\"When Love Kills Love\\", appears to be the most popular of the new songs.  The band is to be complemented for taking risks, but they do not fare quite as well on some of the cover tunes.  The tempo of \\"Dust In the Wind\\" is a little too brisk, and while Klaus Meine is unquestionably a great singer, he doesn't have quite the right voice for the song.  Likewise, he lacks the subtly to handle the Cars' \\"Drive\\".<br /><br />The production of Acoustica is first class, and features very good image quality and a number of audio options.  The square shaped stage is quite spacious, and provides some atypical views of the musicians.  Camera coverage of the band is pretty good, and includes feeds from mobile cameras suspended over the audience.  Editing is a little fast, but there are a lot of people on stage, and the cutting is mostly sensible and not too annoying.  Probably by design, the front rows of the audience seem to consist mostly of young women.  While the Acoustica DVD contains 21 songs, the audio CD release contains only 15 songs.  For those inNorth America, be sure to get the Region 1 DVD.<br /><br />Acoustica features the band during a time when they seem to be searching for a direction.  If like your music hard and heavy, and don't care for the \\"unplugged\\" thing, you may not appreciate the subtlety of this performance, which provides an opportunity to really hear the nuances of Klaus Meine's voice.  To the delight of most of their long time fans, the Scorpions returned to their heavy metal ways with the release of their next album [[ASIN:B000294T2O Unbreakable]] (2004), and have continued in this direction on their subsequent releases.  The band is apparently in the process of completing their \\"farewell tour\\", but hopefully their contributions to music, either as a band or as individual musicians, will continue for many years to come.North America, be sure to get the Region 1 DVD.<br /><br />Acoustica features the band during a time when they seem to be searching for a direction.  If like your music hard and heavy, and don't care for the \\"unplugged\\" thing, you may not appreciate the subtlety of this performance, which provides an opportunity to really hear the nuances of Klaus Meine's voice.  To the delight of most of their long time fans, the Scorpions returned to their heavy metal ways with the release of their next album [[ASIN:B000294T2O Unbreakable]] (2004), and have continued in this direction on their subsequent releases.  The band is apparently in the process of completing their \\"farewell tour\\", but hopefully their contributions to music, either as a band or as individual musicians, will continue for many years to come.

B006ZT47O0|4.0|First of all...Simone's voice. Wow. In this release, we hear more mid-range than high notes...and Simone's voice has never sounded better! Is there any style in which she can't sing? From the mellow Delirium, to the in-your-face Serenade of Self-Destruction, her range, flexibility, and skill never fail to be jaw-droppingly stupendous. She switches seamlessly from heart-melting, operatic notes to aggressive snarls that you almost don't notice until they punch you in the face. What struck me most, however, was the sheer, raw emotion she conveyed overall. There were moments in Serenade of Self-Destruction that sent chills down my spine; as for Twin Flames...words cannot describe it.<br /><br />That doesn't mean, however, that Simone's voice was the only good part of the release. The lyrics are a work of art in and of themselves! The fact that the band puts as much thought into them as the music itself is one of the reasons I keep coming back to Epica. DYU metaphorically deconstructed the workings of the universe. RFTI builds on that. The message is clearly there: It is not enough to live in this world. We must open our eyes, and be aware, not only of the truth of our own lives, but also that of others. Ignorance is not an excuse for shifting the blame for the many things wrong with the world, and inaction.<br /><br />It is true that I did not find the riffs to be as memorable as the ones on DYU, but only slightly less so. Even given this, the album grew on me after a while. There are also more growls on RFTI than there were on the previous releases, which perhaps is reminiscent of MaYaN's Quarterpast. I, personally, have no problem with this, as I very much enjoyed that album as well. I like the death metal texture to Epica's music, and it's why I choose Epica: the so-called \\"Beauty and the Beast\\" vocal combination, with a brutal side serving of metal! I listen to Epica for just this sort of thing, a death metal opera sound that I have not found anywhere else. If I want straight symphonic metal with all clean vocals, I stick to bands like Nightwish, Xandria, Within Temptation, and Delain.<br /><br />Stylistically, there is more of a progressive influence present on this release; the ever-shifting time signatures, musical textures, and clean/growled vocals weave the songs together into a bombastic tapestry of operatic, melodic, classical, death metal, symphonic, progressive...awesomeness.<br /><br />To sum up, no, this album is not Design Your Universe V 2.0, and to be honest, I was a little disappointed that this album wasn't as good as DYU and The Divine Conspiracy. However, it would be difficult indeed to top the epic epicness of Epica's last album, which set the bar sky high. So why did I give it 4 stars? It's because, considered on its own, Requiem for the Indifferent is still a good album in its own right. It is evident that Epica's style, musically, vocally, and message, is evolving. The only constant is change; it's only natural. It's certainly different; all I can say is, I like it on its own. I would recommend giving this a listen.

That's it. B00756GKBA|5.0|Overall, MDNA provides a fantastic return to the music scene for Madonna and will go down as bright spot in an already illustrious career.  The title perfectly sums up how the music has the M(adonna)-DNA - there are throwbacks to classic Madonna tracks with a taste of what the future holds for her. MDNA has Madonna doing what she does best - lighting up the dance floor, opening a window into her life, and boldly trying something new on her own terms.  I'm glad to report after a few listens that Madonna sounds more reinvigorated than ever!<br /><br />Girl Gone Wild - This song has been a major grower for me. It comes packed with awesome beats that are ready for the dance floor. While not the best track here, it's great in context with the album as a whole, and the Act of Contrition opening is epic (and a fitting way to start the album). Madonna is a master at using visuals to get her message across - if you haven't seen the hot black and white video for this song, go watch it now! It's a great throwback to the Madonna of Vogue/Erotica/Human Nature. The song is pretty fun.<br /><br />Gang Bang<br />LOVE this track - it's by far the most unique thing Madonna has done since Music's 'Paradise (not for me).' Madonna sing/talks over a hard, throbbing, industrial beat, violently describing how she's going to shoot her lover - very dark stuff here. I was quite surprised that William Orbit produced this track - it shows a major departure for what you're used to from both him and Madonna.<br /><br />I'm Addicted<br />Another great dance track, I'm Addicted beckons you to get into the groove.  There's a cool urgency in both the lyrics and Madonna's delivery that I really enjoy. This would easily be popular in the clubs.<br /><br />Turn Up the Radio<br />This is the most radio friendly track. It's light and fun and all about moving on and getting away from the things that hold you back. I hope it's released as the next single. It's the perfect summer anthem. While not my personal favorite, I love hearing Madonna sound so happy in a song. Also, I'm a big fan of remixes, and I imagine some cool djs could go crazy with this song. I could have even seen this being a strong lead single.<br /><br />Give Me All Your Luvin<br />Unlike some people, I love this song. It's simple, catchy, and fun as hell. I don't think it ranks as Madonna's strongest lead single by any means, but it's great fun, especially in context with the other songs on the album. Knowing next to nothing about Nicki Minaj and MIA, I enjoy their small raps too. For me, their parts made the song much more interesting and unique.  The exuberance in this track is contagious.<br /><br />Some Girls<br />This is perhaps the biggest surprise for me. I don't know why, but I didn't expect to like it as much as I do. Love the production from Orbit, and I love how Madonna sounds flying through this tune, telling us how some girls will never be like her - how true! It reminds me a little of 'She's Not Me' from Hard Candy, but I think this track is better.<br /><br />Superstar<br />While sugary sweet, this song isn't my favorite of the bunch. Lots of other reviewers have compared it to 'True Blue,' which I can easily understand. Like a friend of mine recently said, even a \\"bad\\" Madonna song is miles better than most of what's out there - and I don't think this is bad by any means .. just not my favorite. Upon further listen, I would move this to the bonus tracks and replace it with \\"Beautiful Killer.\\"<br /><br />I Don't Give A<br />Great beat, great urgency throughout with a vivid, personal look into Madonna's life. She sings fast, in a sort of rap in much of the song. As with 'Like it Or Not' from the Confessions album, Madonna sings about doing her best and not caring what others think, which I appreciate.  The Minaj rap fits in well.<br /><br />I'm A Sinner<br />Production-wise, this Orbit track sounds like a mix between 'Beautiful Stranger' and 'Amazing.' It's miles better than 'Amazing' and probably as good as 'Beautiful Stranger.' Madonna's vocals start off sounding quite strange - very high and thin, but it's fitting. Vocally, I feel like Madonna's taking a major risk here by trying something new. This song would make a pretty awesome single too - it's catchy as hell and provocative.  Again, Madonna sounds like she's having a lot of fun.<br /><br />Love Spent<br />Damn, a Madonna song with banjo!! This, along with the acoustic version, makes me hope for an all acoustic album from Madonna one day! Another very personal track, probably about her past marriage. There's a feeling of deep longing here. The arrangement of this song is quite unique too. I can see why it's a fan favorite.<br /><br />Masterpiece<br />I wasn't sure this Golden Globe Award winning song would fit into the album, but I'm pleasantly surprised that it does. In the context of the album, this is a great track, a sort of slow down from so many heavy dance beats. It's a nice ballad that harkens back to Madonna's Ray of Light days. There's a sadness here that Madonna does so well. Vocally, she sounds great - people can say what they want about Madonna's vocal abilities, but few artists out there can emote like she does.  This song is running over with emotion.<br /><br />Falling Free<br />This strange slow song ends the album on a melancholy note, much like \\"Easy Ride\\" did with American Life.  I prefer \\"Easy Ride,\\" but this song is growing on me.  In comparison with the rest of the record, it's such a simple song in regards to production and instrumentation.  The style also reminds me of \\"Mer Girl\\" from Ray of Light.<br /><br />Beautiful Killer<br />The first of the bonus tracks, I love this song! It should be on the main album, replacing \\"Superstar.\\" A portion reminds me of \\"Die Another Day,\\" a song I love. It's got a great chorus that really sticks in your head.  Out of all the songs here, this one really has that classic Madonna feel, so I'm surprised it's not a part of the main set. I could even see it being a successful single.<br /><br />I F***** Up<br />Not a bad song, but I kind of wish Madonna would have changed it to \\"I Messed Up.\\" The vulgarity of the \\"F\\" word in the title is a bit of a turnoff for me. Otherwise, it's not bad.  Again, Madonna gets really personal here, describing all the ways she messed up with a an important relationship. I like the cheeky ending that makes you wonder if she REALLY thinks it was all her fault.<br /><br />B-Day Song<br />This song has a cool 60s vibe, and I like the simple sound. It seems like Madonna and MIA just sat around and banged this out on the fly, much like the early version of \\"I Love New York\\" on the Re-Invention concert album sounds. While fun, I can see why it didn't make the main album.<br /><br />Best Friend<br />Another personal song about Madonna's failed marriage to Guy Ritchie (or, that's the assumption, anyway). Again, not a bad track, but I can see why it didn't make it on the main album.<br /><br />MDNA is a great blend of what Madonna does best. While it's too early for me to say how it'll rank overall, I already like it much better than her last album, Hard Candy (which I like, but don't love). MDNA is a cool mix of Ray of Light meets Confessions on a Dancefloor with a little Music thrown in - and even some throwbacks to the Erotica days.  It's amazing to me that an artist that has been around this long is still putting out such quality music - people should really respect that. The sequencing of songs could be improved, however. A track like \\"Gang Bang\\" should not show up so early in the set .. there should be more of a lead up to a song like that.

B0074EIQQU|5.0|As a precaution, I thought it was important to note that when it comes to The Mars Volta, I tend to get very emotionally immersed in the music of each new album which sometimes makes it difficult for me to judge the merits of the album objectively until later, when I've taken a good break away from it. To this day, I still see De-Loused in the Comatorium as a flawless classic, and Frances the Mute, despite all of its grandiosity, is a very solid effort as well. The Bedlam in Goliath was an explosive rebound to the disappointing Amputechture, and its chaotic and urgent atmosphere took hold of me like a victim of musical Stockholm Syndrome in that I was enamored with the album for weeks and was unable to judge it fairly until I broke free. Afterwards, I came to the decision that while it's a good album, it's a bit too overwhelming for regular listening and a lot of the songs become redundant after a while. The more somber tone of Octahedron coincided with a time in my life in which I was experiencing some deep emotional turmoil, and while the album was on constant repeat for a few weeks during that time, it is now hard to listen to the opening track \\"Since We've Been Wrong\\" without a feeling of bitterness. Aside from my own personal reactions, I would still consider Octahedron a bit too melancholic to be one of TMV's best. I would say the only TMV album that has thoroughly disappointed me right from the get-go, however, would be Amputechture, whose scatterbrained overindulgence makes for a very tedious listen. If I do listen to it, I skip right past \\"Vicarious Atonement,\\" and really, every other track after that.<br /><br />Now moving to the present - Noctourniquet. At the moment, I have this album on repeat and I'm very into it, but I don't think I'm jumping the gun when I say this may very well be their best effort since De-Loused. However, I said the same thing about The Bedlam in Goliath, so I may be revising this review later, but as I perceive it right now, it may very well be the most balanced and consistent TMV album to come out in a while. I had my reservations considering the absence of John Frusciante (one of my all-time favorite guitarists), Ikey Owens, and Thomas Pridgen, but in retrospect, it seems like this stripped down version of The Mars Volta is exactly what was needed. Deantoni Parks takes a break from the fast-paced and bombastic drumming styles of Jon Theodore and Thomas Pridgen to offer a more straight-forward drumming style, while still adding some nice fills here and there, which I think helps the album flow more smoothly. Omar has stated that his playing of all guitar and keyboards on this album has allowed to consider a more balanced position for both the instruments, as opposed to the wall of guitar sound that has often drowned out Ikey Owens' keyboards in the past.<br /><br />Songs like \\"The Whip Hand,\\" \\"Lapochka,\\" and \\"Zed and Two Naughts\\" are all electronic-heavy, which adds a great new perspective on TMV's classic sound, while \\"Dyslexicon\\" and \\"Molochwalker\\" sound like traditional TMV and would have not been too out of place on De-Loused in the Comatorium or Frances the Mute.  \\"Empty Vessels Make the Loudest Sound\\" and \\"Trinkets Pale of Moon\\" are slower, more melancholy tracks that would have fit in on Octahedron - and both seem reminiscent of King Crimson, who have been a major inspiration for the band. \\"In Absentia\\" and \\"Imago\\" trigger thoughts of German krautrock band CAN, who have influenced the band as well. \\"The Malkin Jewel\\" is an amazing track and is unlike anything heard in TMV's back catalogue; I think it exemplifies the \\"future punk\\" sound that Cedric was talking about and I hope to hear more songs like this from TMV in the future. The other tracks all find their place within the album and contribute to an intriguing and varied listening experience, while still maintaining consistency and a smooth flow.<br /><br />While I consider De-Loused in the Comatorium to be TMV's classic, holdingNoctourniquet to that standard might seem a little unfair, as TMV has come a long way since their debut album. But when compared to more recent albums, I think this album is a great step out of the stale and overindulgent prog-metal sound that the band had started to become entrenched in, and quite frankly, it's a lot more enjoyable of a listen. The band has shown that it isn't afraid to go outside of its comfort zone and make a more straight-forward album that still experiments and doesn't compromise artistic integrity - actually, it promotes artistic integrity. Omar has defined this album as \\"the end of an era\\" and states that all future albums will be a more collaborative process. Now that TMV has fully regained my interest, I'm intrigued to see where they will go from here.<br /><br />Best tracks: The Malkin Jewel, The Whip Hand, Empty Vessels Make the Loudest Sound, Molochwalker.Noctourniquet to that standard might seem a little unfair, as TMV has come a long way since their debut album. But when compared to more recent albums, I think this album is a great step out of the stale and overindulgent prog-metal sound that the band had started to become entrenched in, and quite frankly, it's a lot more enjoyable of a listen. The band has shown that it isn't afraid to go outside of its comfort zone and make a more straight-forward album that still experiments and doesn't compromise artistic integrity - actually, it promotes artistic integrity. Omar has defined this album as \\"the end of an era\\" and states that all future albums will be a more collaborative process. Now that TMV has fully regained my interest, I'm intrigued to see where they will go from here.<br /><br />Best tracks: The Malkin Jewel, The Whip Hand, Empty Vessels Make the Loudest Sound, Molochwalker.

0385534639|5.0|Marco and Celia are pitted against each other in a mysterious game they have been preparing for since they were children. Le Cirque des Rves is the staging ground - a magical circus full of wonders.<br /><br />The Night Circus seems to be one of those books that people either love or hate, judging by the reviews I've seen. The story is quite slow to develop. The main characters don't even see each other for years at a time and compete by adding wonders to the circus to out-do each other. If you're after a battle with Cruciatus curses flying around, you're in the wrong place.<br /><br />I loved reading this book. It's hard to put into words why I did, but I think the descriptions of the Cirque is what did it for me - Morgenstern's gift for beautiful prose is undeniable and she conjures dream-like images from every page. I may just have to get myself a red scarf and become a rveur!<br /><br />Set in and around the late 1800s, the story is made up of many small chapters, switching between several different threads of story. At first this was a little confusing  because some sections are later in time than others, but once I started paying attention to the dates at the start of each section I understood better how all the threads fit together. Another potentially confusing element is that it is told in the present tense. It took me a little while to get used to it, then every now and then there is a section of second-person point of view (for example, \\"You move the curtain aside\\") which allows Morgenstern to describe a tent that the characters haven't visited.<br /><br />As the story moves on, the threads become shorter and closer together, until they are woven together into one story. The story itself does peter out a little at the end, the action giving way to a lengthy discussion between characters in the last few chapters.<br /><br />The author has created a cast of interesting characters, complete with a web of relationships. The romance is sweet and delightful, although there isn't really any explanation as to why it exists. That didn't stop it from sending tingles up my spine while reading, though.<br /><br />Erin Morgenstern's debut is a delight to read. If you love magic and descriptions of beautiful and fantastic places, read The Night Circus without delay!, although there isn't really any explanation as to why it exists. That didn't stop it from sending tingles up my spine while reading, though.<br /><br />Erin Morgenstern's debut is a delight to read. 1932100660|5.0|I'm 2/3 through a book called \\"The China Study\\" by  T Colin Campbell, Ph.D., an icon in the field of micro-biology and nutritional medicine.  The book reflects the culmination of 27 years of analytic research, all peer reviewed and published in all the right journals of medicine, into the associations of diet and Western Diseases - including all the cancers, heart disease, diabetes (1 and 2), and obesity. His research was triangular: Molecular laboratory studies, laboratory studies with rats and mice, and the most comprehensive epidemiological study on nutrition and disease ever conducted - which is the title of the book - the China Study.<br /><br />I'll touch on the lab study with rats and mice, whose findings were confirmed by the other two types of studies. The livers of thousands of rats were injected with Aflatoxin, a highly toxic carcinogen. Then they were separated into two groups - one group was fed a diet of which 5% of calorie intake was animal protein (casein).  The diet of the second group consisted of 20% animal protein. The normal life span of the rats is 2 years.  Within 18 months, 100% of the rats fed the second diet were dead or dying of cancer of the liver, while 0% of the first group died of this disease.  Dr Campbell's group was astonished, as a 0 to 100% result almost never happens, so they did the study again, and again, and again, scores of times.  They then decided to use a different specie, using mice instead, and got the exact same results.<br /><br />In the China Study, the epidemiological study that extended not only to China but to the Phillipines, Indonesia, and other Asian countries, the research group learned that there appears to be a one-to-one correlation between eating a Western diet (meats, dairy, eggs) and the incidence of cancers, heart disease, diabetes, and obesity.  Again, in regions where greater amounts of animal protein are part of the diet, they found greater incidence of Western Disease.  And the more animal protein people ate, the more the incidence of these diseases, the less animal protein they ate, the less incidence of such diseases.<br /><br />I believe that if you read just the first 69 pages, the first 3 chapters, you won't be able to put the book down. It's one of those life changing books.

So much for the \\"low intellect\\" argument<br /><br />Then there is this from the internet:<br /><br />\\"Why the mathematicians, more than other scientists, tend to believe there's a God<br />Of all scientists, mathematicians are most inclined to believe in God. - A finding of Professor Edward Larson of the University of Georgia and Larry Witham of Bartonsville, Maryland, in a survey of 600 scientists, as reported by the London Weekly Telegraph.<br /><br />In 1916, Professor James Leuba of Bryn Mawr University in Pennsylvania surveyed the religious beliefs of scientists. He found that about 42% believed in God, almost exactly the same percentage did not, and another 16% described themselves as doubtful about God, although not convinced of his non-existence. In short, about 40% could be described as believers and 60% as unbelievers.<br /><br />The Leuba survey created a sensation. Politicians expressed fears that university science courses would lead young people away from religion. Prof. Leuba himself envisioned a continuing trend away from God, so that by the end of the century few if any scientists would be believers.<br /><br />Therefore, with the year 2000 close at hand, Prof. Larson and Mr. Witham conducted a matching survey. Had the Leuba prophecy come true? They found it had not. Belief and non-belief among scientists had not significantly changed. The total expressing belief was 39.3%, while 45.3% listed themselves as unbelievers and 14.5% as doubtful. The 60-40 ratio held.<br /><br />This assumes, of course, that it has remained consistent throughout the century. It may not have. Prof. Leuba may have been right for a time as the number of believing scientists continued to shrink, but the trend may have later reversed.<br /><br />The Larson-Witham survey did turn up some unexpected changes. Three disciplines were examined: physicists, biologists and mathematicians. In Prof. Leuba's day, the most determined unbelievers were the biologists (69.5%). Today it's the physicists and astronomers, 77.9% of whom list themselves as such. Biologists, meanwhile, seem to have somewhat recovered their faith, though the Telegraph story did not cite a specific percentage.<br /><br />The relatively improved faith of biologists may well be due to the gradual decline in credibility of Darwin's theory of natural selection. Too many holes have appeared in it, and biologists would be the first to become aware of this. They would know before anyone else, for instance, of the failure to discover the fossil remains of transitional species, of the failure of laboratory experiment to duplicate any evolutionary change and, most recently,of the profound complexities evidenced in the single cell, which Darwin regarded as \\"the simple cell.\\"<br /><br />But it seems that faith is strongest today among the mathematicians, 44.6% describing themselves as definitely believing that behind reality there must be some kind of Mind. Wondering about this, we consulted two friends, one a retired physicist, the other a young mathematician. Both are believers. Why, we asked, would mathematicians be more prone to believe?<br /><br />The physicist's answer went like this: \\"I suspect it comes from the role mathematics plays in the exploration of the solar system. After all, using nothing more complex than Newtonian mathematics, the mathematician calculates the necessities of sending a rocket from here to Venus where it orbits and gathers thrust from the rotation of that planet, then comes back and circles Earth, gathering further thrust from our planet, then goes to Jupiter and takes up a precisely calculated position around that planet. All on the basis of simple Newtonian maths. The mathematician marvels at this. He begins to see mathematics, not as a mere humanly contrived system, but as a great work of art by a great Creator, and he is awestruck.\\"<br /><br />The mathematician, Mike Roshko of Edmonton, graduated in pure mathematics from the University of Alberta two years ago, found there were no jobs to be had in this line, and is now a computer programmer in Ottawa. He answered this way:<br /><br />\\"For me, it's amazing the way in which the seemingly different areas of mathematics fit together. When you begin studying advanced math, you tend to think of geometry, algebra, analysis and so on as separate entities, each beautiful and elegant on its own.<br /><br />\\"But as you go on, you realize that these different areas are connected in the most astonishing yet natural ways. You may discover that what you thought of as purely a part of geometry turns out to be an essential part of algebra. And what we're dealing with is not just something we've made up. It's a reality. It's there.<br /><br />\\"And it all intertwines and works so perfectly, so beautifully, that you realize that Somebody or Something must have done this. It simply could not have happened by chance. It's a kind of revelation, I guess. And it's very convincing.\\"<br /><br />Addition:<br /><br />Now they say never to argue with people over religion, it seems that my review has alienated SOME atheists, in that it contains some arguments in support of a designer and the names of some great minds who believe in one.<br /><br />Additionally, the review has also irritated some believers who believe with ABSOLUTE certainty that there is a God. 0525423656|3.0|WARNING! SPOILERS AHEAD!<br /><br />In my review of Matched, I made a mention of the fact that I was \\"eager\\" to read Crossed \\"despite\\" the reviews I had read. And I was, I really was. The problem? I should have listened when every single one of them said-in one way or another-that nothing happened.<br /><br />Alright, I'm getting quite snappy and far ahead of myself. I was excited to pick up Crossed, because I thought Matched carried so much promise. Before 100 pages had gone by, however, I was quite disappointed. My first shocker was that the book kept switching back and forth between Ky and Cassia as narrators. Yes, yes, I see that the blurb mentions that, but I didn't read it before I dove right in. I probably should have, but what can I say? The back and forth got quite choppy in places, and as Ky and Cassia met up again it got fairly bulky. Some of those chapters seemed like they were just thrown in so that a chapter break could be had in between (mostly) Cassia's viewpoint.<br /><br />My second problem was the apparent ADD the book had developed. Now, I don't mind flashbacks when they're done properly but this...wasn't it. Both Cassia and Ky were jumping in and out of the past and present with almost no warning, leaving my jolted out of the writing and thoroughly confused. This was heavily prevalent in the front of the book, disappeared in the middle and showed up once or twice again in the end. It was a very, very messy use of flashbacks that left me rather annoyed.<br /><br />The thing about Crossed is that it really wasn't a book. Sure, there was a vague plotline taking place, but if I was being kind I'd call it filler in between Matched and the final and yet untitled third book. It was barely even that. None of it made sense and none of it felt right.<br /><br />*END SPOILERS*<br /><br />Overall, Crossed was a huge disappointment. I really, really wanted to like this book, but it just defeated my attempts at every turn. 0142419400|5.0|When I started this blog, I swore I would be analytical. I swore that I would look at a book with a critical eye no matter how much I enjoyed the storyline. Since then, I've done that. Or at least, I think I have. (Drop me a line if you think there's a way for me to improve my reviews!) Either way, if you like a critical book review...stop reading here. Almost nothing in this book is going to be critical. I am going to allow myself to be the 17 year old girl that I am and just...gush.<br /><br />Because I loved this book.<br /><br />I'll admit, I nearly gave this book 4  stars simply for the fact that I don't want to be one of those people who throws around 5 star ratings. But then I stopped and thought...why? There is absolutely and utterly no reason.<br /><br />I should start this off with a disclaimer: I usually HATE books that are entirely teen romance. I hate them. I literally hate them. It's like all YA authors think that these things need to be filled with a bunch of clich&eacute;s and fantasy. (Disagree? Comment and give me a book as an example!) When you pick up Anna and the French Kiss, the synopsis doesn't seem promising. Girl goes to boarding school, girl meets guy, they fall in love, PLAY THE SAPPY HAPPY ENDING! It is the plot of ten dozen different teen novels with the same exact premise as this one.<br /><br />But that is not what happened here.<br /><br />Anna and the French Kiss was REAL. In some YAs--and this is especially horrible in the first person, as Anna and the French Kiss is written--the main character is clearly being written by an adult. There are a myriad of ways that this shows itself, but all us teens know it. During this book, however, Anna was either absolutely and utterly exactly like me or at least a girl I would kill to have as my best friend. She was actually a teen like me, who thought like me and talked like me and related in every which way to me. Even if this book hadn't had some other amazing qualities, I could have liked it just on that alone. But it got better.<br /><br />The plot was REAL. Alright, it was fairly fairytale, what with the Paris setting and the hot English guy, but I'll forget about that for now. Anna was not a sad, swoony girl who knew that she and Etienne were soul mates from the first second. Etienne did not fall in love with her at first glance, nor was he a jerk who changes his ways because of her or some other clich&eacute;. He was a real guy. She was a real girl. They both had their issues that weren't just limited to their families (though there was certainly some fairly clich&eacute; family/father drama). They both had their own personality issues, and they both made some choices and had views that weren't necessarily correct.<br /><br />Hallelujah for an author who gets it.<br /><br />Alright, the ending is pretty fairytale. They all live happily ever after in the most swoon worthy fashion. That didn't bother me all that much. Maybe a little bit of fairytale isn't that bad after all. The plot was real enough and I loved the characters so much that I honestly wanted that happily ever after. Despite its premise and ending, though, Anna and the French Kiss has been an answer to my prayers. It's a teen romance I can stomach, has a main character that's real and has a love story that's parameters weren't set up by the Brothers Grimm. It's well written, it's cute, it's funny and it's REAL. I hear that Perkins's next book, Lola and the Boy Next Door (on shelves now), has a more realistic setting and I am jumping up and down to get a hold of it. Anna and the French Kiss isn't just a good read; it's my new best friend.t on that alone. But it got better.<br /><br />The plot was REAL. It's a teen romance I can stomach, has a main character that's real and has a love story that's parameters weren't set up by the Brothers Grimm. It's well written, it's cute, it's funny and it's REAL. People are so caught up in this game-like way of life they scarcely notice what's going on outside. OASIS creator James Halliday has just died, and though he is the world's wealthiest man, he's also a hermit who left behind no heirs. He left behind an elaborate contest within the OASIS in which anyone and everyone can search for a hidden easter egg, and whoever finds it will inherit his vast fortune as well as control of his company. Millions set off in search of the egg, and when the novel begins the search has been underway for about five years, and nobody has yet found even the first of three keys, which will open the three gates (also hidden) which are necessary to obtain the egg.<br /><br />The above may sound like spoilers but this is basically the setup within the first few pages, and the story proceeds from there. We meet Wade Watts, a young \\"egg hunter,\\" and follow his interactions with others on the same quest.<br /><br />The quest itself is entertaining, but the real thing going on here is that James Halliday, a child of the 1980s, has sprinkled throughout the message he left behind announcing the contest a large number of hints and red herrings all taken from 80s pop culture -- dialog from John Hughes movies, lyrics from an Oingo Boingo song and more. There are a few cultural tidbits on focus here which are outside my own historical interest -- never much of a Black Tiger player here -- but far more elements I recognize from my own trip through the decade of my adolescence. Arcade games like Tempest, Pac Man, Joust and Battlezone, movies like Blade Runner and Monty Python's Holy Grail... the music, the Dungeons and Dragons. Such a lot of fun here! This is one of those books I want to recommend to anybody and everybody within five years of my age (those born in the 60s), and it might even be fun for people outside that range.<br /><br />All Ernest Cline seems to have done before this book was to write the screenplay for the film Fanboys, a sort of trial run for the sort of geek obsessions on display here. I can't wait to see what he does next, and fully expect to read this book again. Highly recommended, unless the kind of cultural references listed above are totally uninteresting to you.Tempest, Pac Man, Joust and Battlezone, movies like Blade Runner and Monty Python's Holy Grail... the music, the Dungeons and Dragons. Such a lot of fun here! B000095IUM|4.0|Beethoven Symphonies 1 - 9. Chamber Orchestra of Europe and the Arnold Schoenberg Choir. With Charlotte Margiono, Rudolf Schasching, Birgit Remmert and Robert Holl. Recorded 1991. Teldec.<br /><br />Harnoncourt's cycle starts off very impressively, aided by superb sound. It is hard to believe that this cycle was recorded live - it has the feel of a spacious studio acoustic. As with Karajan and Solti, Harnoncourt treats the First with just as much vitality and strength as the more mature symphonies: the tempi are solid not rushed and the instruments have a beautiful sheen to them, whilst never sacrificing body. The climaxes are just that - not the trashy bashing of a drum which so often disfigures Norrington's earlier period performances. I particularly liked the middle movements in this recording: the splendid playing is balanced with knife-edged drama and really spot-on tempos. The same is true of the Second: Harnoncourt really makes a dramatic statement about the piece and the result is really electrifying.<br /><br />Undoubtedly any performance of the Eroica will have to bring out its harsh edges at times - especially in the first movement. Harnoncourt particularly excels in those moments - the characterisation of the first two movements is very powerful: dramatic and almost violent without being vulgar. Sometimes more repose is required in the marche funebre, but it all comes off quite nicely - the credit also due to the continued excellent playing of the Chamber Orchestra of Europe.<br /><br />The Fourth does not quite equal the some of its parts. It starts out very beautifully and with a real sense of mystery, but much of it is a bit all over the place. I didn't really feel a cohesive vision. The slow movement was a particular movement - not as beautiful as it can be. Tempos were a bit erratic and the playing less refined than elsewhere in the cycle.<br /><br />The Fifth is certainly a strong performance: tempi are never rushed and you don't feel like the whole thing descends into farce like the one in Norrington's cycle. The superior playing from Harnoncourt's forces also make it streets ahead of Norrington's version. I would probably rate this Fifth in front of Karajan's and Solti's 1970s recordings as well. At times, you might feel that the performance is just a little too hard pressed - but  I don't really object: I think the tension and uplift of that final glorious movement is well caught. What I like is that nothing feels 'clipped' in this version and it is also not rushed - a great boon. Still, it fails to displace Bernstein 1961 as my all time favourite recording of this great work.<br /><br />The Harnoncourt Sixth is another completely satisfying performance. It may be surprising how the first two movements are quite slow. I personally think the pace throughout the symphony is well judged. The central movements are accelerated, but the beauty of the symphony is always foremost. But I wouldn't call it the most dramatic or tense account of this elusive masterpiece. I think Karajan, for all of his detractors in the Sixth, captures those qualities more than any other (except perhaps Bernstein).<br /><br />Harnoncourt exploits every possible dynamic contrast and instrumental detail in the Seventh. It is a richly dramatic reading and the octane level just keeps rising as the symphony moves through its third and fourth movement. The very last, the allegro con brio, is played here better than any other recording I have - the conducting and the playing are simply inspired. For once you feel that everything is just right in this movement and the joy and attraction of this amazing movement is really exploited. Earlier, however, I find that some of the playing is scrappy and the strings thin. Still, it's all quite involving. For period enthusiasts this clearly outmatches the Norrington in every way (as usual).<br /><br />The performance that most strikes me in this cycle is the unassuming Eighth. It is given a marvelous performance here. Whilst the playing isn't as good as that of the Berlin Philharmonic, for example, it makes up for that with a really outlandish account. It is lively and elegant and always surprising.<br /><br />Like the other period performance of this symphony with which I am familiar (the Norrington), this ranks as the low point in Harnoncourt's otherwise solid cycle. It is bland and uninspired, capped off by uninvolved contributions from the four soloists in the finale. It could very well be that this symphony requires something deeper than scholarship and fizzy tempos. These conductors seem to overlook this symphony and treat it like it's just a run-through rather than one of the cornerstones of symphonic literature. For a truly inspired account, one is urged to go to Furtwangler's Bayreuth 'vision' above all, followed closely by Solti and then Karajan in his 1977 account. They convey something of the perfection that this symphony represents.<br /><br />Overall, then, this is quite a good cycle. Originally, I thought it to be rather boring. On second hearing, it strikes you as being quite fresh and spontaneous without sacrificing either nuance or some of the grand old tried and true methods of conventional performance (hence the title of this review). This proves the importance of listening more than once to cycles like these. Unlike Norrington's ghastly approach in many of these works, there is genuine respect and feeling for the spirit of Beethoven in most of the works. With the exception of the Fourth and, more seriously, the Ninth, this cycle is a safe bet for first timers, but an even stronger recommendation for seasoned collectors who have yet to visit the period 'scene'. But because the Ninth is so piecemeal, I couldn't give it a full five star rating. Four stars then.rformance here. B00004W510|5.0|Well, since so many have already written such superb reviews and analytical essays on this album, I must say straight that my only excuse in adding my two cents here is that this being such a favourite of mine and having reviewed other favourites of mine on Amazon, I feel a kind of obligation to myself...<br />Sorry for the long prelude; here I go:<br /><br />With my 'Music From Big Pink' review I focused on how great the addition of the bonus tracks are. Since this isn't so much the case here(although they're interesting and it's worth hearing the studio version of 'Get Up Jake') I shall have to work the main feature; the album: It's perfect, really, no matter how you look at it. Probably even from a mathematical perspective.<br />Big Pink, their first album and masterpiece, is equally perfect but what is interesting is that although the production and consistency of song and sound is so exquisitly captured on The Band(or \\"Brown Album\\") and 'Big Pink' is quite raw and sprawling(part of its beauty) it doesn't, in my opinion, supersede or top their debut; it cements it really.<br /><br />Their trademark switching of vocals and instruments works to stunning effect on both and the timeless warmth and aching soul runs particularly rampant through the first two albums like a benevolent musical virus, but on their second we really see the alchemy full-frontal and clear as a sunny Autumn day in the woods.<br />I don't know of many bands that can mix around the duties of their personnel so often and yet keep the personality of the group sound and identity so completely intact:<br />Levon might switch to mandolin while Manuel flaps about on the drums; Garth shows the world that, yes, he can also play the rag-time piannie like he invented it; Danko scratches out a beautifully raw violin riff, besides his air-shifting bass and Robbie writes a perfect song as any while playing guitar like a groovy scientist; then they'll play musical chairs again and we'll be blessed with a ballad so gorgeous from Richard Manuel that we would drink it too, if we could, while weeping tears of poignant joy.<br /><br />It is commonly stated that there was a particularly 'woody' sound to the drums on this album, and that analogy can probably be expanded to describe the overall sound of it; grainy, earthy... you know: rustic. But there is not a note out of place; not a sloppy or lazy moment to behold. It is mastery of the form... but what form? Folk, Blues, Country, Soul, Rock 'n' Roll... Americana?<br />The Band.lad so gorgeous from Richard Manuel that we would drink it too, if we could, while weeping tears of poignant joy.<br /><br />It is commonly stated that there was a particularly 'woody' sound to the drums on this album, and that analogy can probably be expanded to describe the overall sound of it; grainy, earthy... you know: rustic. Slow down! The band feels the need to speed up the tempo of songs that were originally recorded at a much slower tempo.  This causes them to sound a bit jumbled live, and Myles loses breath just slightly. 'Find The Real' and 'Slip To The Void', two of my favorites, encompass this.  Both are great songs, both sound good live, but I wish they would have played them at the right tempo.<br /><br />2.) How 'bout some different songs? But they should have performed some songs that weren't on the Amsterdam release. I didn't particularly care to hear 'Come to Life, 'Ties That Bind', and 'Broken Wings' again. Swearing. I'm not the first reviewer to note this, but I feel it bears repeating. I am by no means a prude, but unexplained f-bombs in random places make Myles sound ridiculous and takes away from the experience. Plus, you can't let your kids watch it...and I'd rather my kids appreciate good rock music instead of Nicki Minaj or Adele.
B0050PYNN0|1.0|Despite all its potential, efforts of lavish special effects, slew of highly talented actors and even seemingly promising trailers, `Your Highness' fails miserably on absolutely every level imaginable, competing with even the Transformers sequels and Jason Friedberg/Aaron Seltzer parody movies (truly ghastly comparisons) for worst movie ever. Hopefully the Razzies are taking notes.<br /><br />Although I shouldn't have to explain the plot (because no one should ever, by any means, see this movie if given the choice), I will anyway for clarity's sake. Set in medieval times, Thadeous (Danny McBride) and his brother Fabious (James Franco) are both the sons of King Tallious and warriors expected to defend their kingdom from evil. While Fabious is beloved by the kingdom and excels in combat, however, Thadeous is lazy, arrogant and more known for his lust for women than slaying any villains. One day Fabious saves the virgin Belladonna (Zooey Deschanel) from a tower, where she was held captive by the evil wizard Leezar (Justin Theroux). Upon bringing her home to marry her, however, Leezar appears and kidnaps her again, attempting to fulfill a prophecy of a warlock impregnating a maiden with a fearsome dragon to attack the kingdom. Random chaos ensues, but trust me when I say there's no need for any explanation beyond that.<br /><br />The film is bogged down by nauseating toilet humor, atrocious writing and juvenile, unfunny gags (unless you're under the age of 15 or a heavily inebriated frat boy, you absolutely won't be laughing once). It also really can't seem to decide what it wants to be; given the blatant tone of the trailers (and opening scenes), you'd expect that the entirety of the film would be a comedy/medieval parody (or at least an attempt at one) along the lines of Monty Python and the Holy Grail. This is only halfway the case, as the movie makes sporadic pleas to be taken seriously, or maybe just desperately hopes to systematically distract viewers from the fact that the `comedy' is gag-inspiringly godawful. These embarrassing attempts at grounded plot are the most laughable moments in the movie.<br /><br />In a particularly foul scene, the grotesque, pedophilic `Great Wise Wizard' (a bizarre Yoda-looking creature) insists that Fabious and Thadeous give him kisses and then a handjob (viewers are subjected to both). Thadeous also spends several minutes toward the end of the film sporting a minotaur's severed penis as a necklace (as if viewer's palettes aren't in need of enough cleansing by that point). How on earth the likes of James Franco and Natalie Portman of all people didn't have anything better to do is beyond me.<br /><br />It's such an utter waste, really and truly, especially considering the genuinely impressive CGI effects in the final scenes. Given the trite material they have to work with, it shouldn't come as a huge surprise that even the handful of supremely talented cast members can't save this atrocity. It's not funny, it's not entertaining, it is absolutely not worth a single person on this earth's time. Buzz Killington should clearly stick to Family Guy cameos, because buzzkill \\"comedy\\" leaves such a nasty aftertaste.

B003Y5H5HY|5.0|The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo Blu-ray Review<br /><br />Year: 2011<br />Rating: R<br />Runtime: 2 HR 38 MIN<br /><br />Director: David Fincher<br />Starring: Daniel Craig, Rooney Mara, Christopher Plummer, Stellan Skarsgrd, Steven Berkoff, Robin Wright, Joely Richardson, and Goran Visnjic<br /><br />Film: 5 out of 5<br />Video: 5 out of 5<br />Audio: 4 out of 5<br />Extras: 5 out of 5<br />Overall: 5 out of 5<br /><br />The Film-<br /><br />David Fincher has directed several of my favorite films of the last twenty years but he's had almost as many misses as he has hits. The Game, Panic Room, and The Curious Case Of Benjamin Button are technically impressive films that I wouldn't qualify as bad but I rarely feel the need to revisit. On the other hand Seven, Fight Club and Zodiac are films that I can watch repeatedly and take away something new on every viewing. Somehow I still haven't seen The Social Network so I can't speak to its successes or failures but I can unequivocally say that The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo will be another Fincher film that I will visit often for years to come.<br /><br />Investigative journalist Mikael Blomkvist (Daniel Craig) has just lost a libel case for an \\"unflattering\\" article he wrote which has put him in and his publisher in financial ruin. Mikael is summoned to a meeting with Henrik Vanger, a wealthy businessman. Henrik presents him with the opportunity to investigate the suspected murder of his niece Harriet almost forty years ago. It soon becomes clear that he is in over his head and needs a second pair of eyes to piece together the mystery. Mikael's employer puts him in contact with Lisbeth, a skilled investigator with a personality as unique as her dragon tattoo.<br /><br />To describe this film as dark doesn't do it justice. The world that Mikael and Lisbeth inhabit is bleak, filled with unsavory characters in both the past and present. Mikael's investigation at first glance may look like the film's main focus but it's actually Lisbeth's story that drives The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo. Her story is weaved throughout Mikael's investigation and while that storyline is more of a procedural her story carries the emotional arc of the story. The film turns convention on its ear by making the strongest character the woman even though because of her circumstances is repeatedly victimized.<br /><br />There are disturbing scenes that will make you squirm and feel uncomfortable; the flip side of that coin is that it's riveting and those scenes payoff in spades later. Fincher never glorifies the violence, but he doesn't shy away from it either. He lets it play out naturally and doesn't edit away the horror; he forces you to look away by just letting the camera roll.<br /><br />While I haven't read the Stieg Larsson novels or seen the original Swedish film to compare to this film I was completely engulfed by Steve Zaillian's script. I purposely avoided the novel and films leading up to the release of the US version so I wouldn't be comparing and contrasting it against its other incarnations. Zaillain's script doesn't fall prey to the pitfalls that usually doom American adaptations such as ham-handedly explaining to the audience what the morale of the story is or tacking on a \\"Hollywood\\" ending to an otherwise good film.<br /><br />David Fincher's team has created an enveloping world that made Sweden feel like its own character. Every shot looks stunning and continues to show why Fincher has one of the best set of eyes in the industry. Trent Reznor & Atticus Ross' moody score blur the line between a conventional film score and something more in tune with rock music. The score is like plugging a pair of headphones into Lisbeth's brain and listening to her internal struggle put to music.<br /><br />All the performances are simply fantastic which isn't unexpected considering what he's been able to do with Brad Pitt (\\"What's in the box!?\\") Even though Daniel Craig gets top billing Rooney Mara is the star and she's simply fantastic. As I mentioned earlier, some horrible things happen to Lisbeth's character and she completely sold me on her portrayal by going all out in her performance. As usual Daniel Craig was very good as well; his character isn't given as much to go through but his performance is still very good. The always great Christopher Plummer and Stellan Skarsgrd also bring \\"A\\" game performances and an elder statesmen touch to the film. Christopher Plummer finally won an Academy Award this year for his role in Beginners but he could have easily won it for The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo as well.<br /><br />This is about as close to a perfect film as you're going to find in this day and age. The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo isn't for the faint of heart. You may see things that you may not want to see but this qualifies as a film where the juice is definitely worth the squeeze.<br /><br />The Disc-<br /><br />The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo is housed inside a cardboard case inside of a cardboard sleeve. I found it difficult to pull the case from the sleeve which has caused the corners of the inside case to look dented and worn. Inside the cardboard case you'll find three discs; one Blu-ray featuring the film, a second Blu-ray with all the special features, and a third disc that is simply a DVD/UltraViolet Digital Copy. If you're a fan of disc art you'll love the artwork or lack thereof on the DVD copy; it simply looks like a standard Sony brand DVD-R with The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo sloppily written across the front which feels quite appropriate for the film<br /><br />In terms of video and audio quality Sony has turned in almost a perfect disc. The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo was shot digitally using a combination of the Red Epic and Red One cameras. The film presentation is flawless; there's not a trace of banding or edge enhancement and black levels are perfectly inky. None of this is a surprise since all of David Fincher films with the exception of The Game and Panic Room have received amazing transfers on Blu-ray.<br /><br />The 5.1 DTS-HD MA lossless soundtrack offers up an extremely engaging experience from the moment the film begins with the James Bond-esque opening sequence. While the film isn't overly action oriented that doesn't mean that the surrounds channels don't create an enveloping experience. Directionality isn't gimmicky but everything from the busy subways to the wind whipping through the frozen woods comes alive. Dialogue is well balanced and is always intelligible which is important because if you were to miss something you could find yourself rewinding. If the soundtrack falters in any way it's in terms of bass which I found to be overpowering. At one point I had to turn down the volume of my entire system because I was concerned about blowing my subwoofers.<br /><br />Disc One's only special feature is the audio commentary by David Fincher. He is one of the few directors I'll listen to just for \\"fun.\\"<br /><br />Disc Two houses all the other special features which are all presented in HD and unless otherwise noted contain a mix of behind the scenes footage and interviews with the cast and crew.<br /><br />-Characters<br />-Salander, Lisbeth<br />Casting Salander<br />Different in Every Way<br />The Look of Salander<br />Mara/Fincher<br />Irene Nesser<br />Salander Test Footage<br />-Blokvist, Mikael<br />Casting Blomkvist<br />Daniel Craig on Film Acting<br />Dressing Blomkvist<br />Investigation (Stills)<br />-Vanger, Martin<br />Stellan Skarsgrd on Film Acting<br />Psychopathy<br />Bondage<br />Torture<br />Wrapped in Plastic<br />Set Design (Stills)<br />-On Location<br />-Sweden<br />Stockholm Syndrome<br />Stockholm's Tennelbana<br />@#$% these People<br />The End<br />Picture Wrap<br />-Hollywood<br />Casting Armansky<br />Armansky Audition<br />Thinking Evil @#$%<br />Rape/Revenge<br />Int.
